## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (driven/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillator models. Typical physics relationships combine a restoring-force term f(x), a damping term g(v), and an external forcing term h(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration, small oscillations about equilibrium)
- Shifted equilibrium oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (x + c1) (linear restoring force around an offset equilibrium position)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator with damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (externally forced damped oscillator)
- Parametric (Mathieu-type) stiffness modulation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric excitation via time-varying stiffness)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with viscous damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (nonlinear spring with forcing)
- Quadratic drag / nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping with direction set by v)
- Mixed linear + quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (combined viscous and drag damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity amplitude)
- Nonlinear restoring via polynomial expansion: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order stiffness terms for strongly nonlinear springs)
- Time-dependent forcing envelope: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + (c2 + c3 * t) * cos(c4 * t + c5) (chirped/slowly varying drive amplitude)
- Liénard-type general oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class with state-dependent damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., c*x + c*x^3), reflecting symmetric potentials about equilibrium.
- Damping sign condition: physical damping typically makes v * dv_dt contain a term that is negative on average (e.g., +c*v with c<0, or -|v|v), ensuring energy dissipation.
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous identification: explicit t-terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t), (c0+c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicate external driving or parametric excitation rather than free oscillation.
- Conservative structure cue: absence of v and t in dv_dt (dv_dt = f(x)) suggests a potential-force model with approximately conserved energy.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency cue: nonlinear stiffness terms (x**3, x**5) imply frequency shifts with amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Limit-cycle cue: state-dependent damping like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v indicates self-excited oscillations that approach a stable limit cycle.
- Drag regime cue: v*Abs(v) terms suggest quadratic drag (higher-speed dissipation) versus linear v for viscous damping (low-speed dissipation).
- Parametric resonance cue: stiffness multiplied by a periodic function of t ( (c0+c1*cos(c*t))*x ) can produce resonance at subharmonics (Mathieu-like behavior).
- Coupled nonlinearity cue: terms like x**2 * v (or general (poly in x)*v) indicate damping that depends on displacement, common in Liénard systems and some mechanical linkages.
